O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles of medical science and its explanations, and have finished it with its interpretations and clarifications. And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of surgery, that is to say "surgery."
And because the practice of surgery is forbidden in our region and is banned altogether, the science has perished and been cut off, and there remains nothing of it outside of the small descriptions in books by ancient authors that have been handled by hands (i.e., used). And it is because of this that errors and falsehoods have arisen, and the intentions have been clouded over and knowledge has been driven away.
It seems to me that I wish to compile together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will compile together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, and the other instruments of the craft along with the description and preparation of them, as is necessary.
And because no skilled craftsmen of hands can be found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected. And it is necessary for one who engages in this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they may know the members (of the body) accurately, and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, veins, and arteries, and the number of them, and the function of those that move and those that rest, and where they originate.
And for this reason Hippocrates said that "the name is much, and the thing (or the reality) is little"; and it is the same in the art of surgery or manual craft.
We tell you at the beginning of this book that he who is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things, let him beware that he does not fall into error and kill men; just as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck and cut the arteries of her neck, causing so much blood to flow out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another physician who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large, but he carried away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
And I had already been called to treat him and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they operated on him, he would die.
And see one other physician who took in charge a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was a wound; and the ignorant physician tightly binds the break over the wound to the splints with great force, and leaves no bandage on the wound, but instead leaves it exposed; and he ordered him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg swelled up completely and the foot became necrotic.
I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind his leg; and when I had undone it, he was relieved and felt no pain.
But the corruption had already spread throughout the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the member until the member was entirely lost.
And I saw another physician who lanced a boil that had become cancerous, and then inflamed it further through the wickedness of his treatment.
For chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in a place where one can completely remove what is corrupt.
And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two branches: namely, work in which there is danger in many ways; and I will point out in every section of this book where there is fear and danger.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that foolish fools cannot speak ill of you.
So take up your weapons in earnestness and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you come to safety and are praised; and leave behind incurable diseases with great care; and put aside your doubts and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other with glory.
Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of serious illnesses, lest you be called a foolish fool."
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medical cauteries, and the chapter is arranged from head to toe; and the forms of instruments, and the iron tools for cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged with the forms of instruments.
The third chapter is about reducing dislocations and sprains, and similar things; and it is arranged from head to toe, and with the forms of instruments
Therefore, so that we remember the work, it is appropriate for me to say the quality of help and harm of each complexion (temperament).
I say that the qualities of help and harm are the longest in speech and the most subtle in knowledge and in hidden responses; and of this, many sages spoke and agreed to it; and I am not satisfied with their words, for I fear lengthiness.
I say that the cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, a hot complexion without matter and a dry complexion without matter.
In a hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have divided and said that the cautery is of great help there; while others have said the opposite: that the cautery is not beneficial for illnesses arising from heat and dryness.
For the nature of fire is hot and should not be used to treat illnesses caused by heat or dryness, as said by those who claim that the cautery provides great help for hot and dry illnesses affecting the body. For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cool.
And I agree with this statement. For I have found it to be true through experience.
And yet, it should not be attempted by anyone other than those who have experienced it and are knowledgeable about the chapter of cauteries, as well as the diversity of human complexions, dispositions, and causes of their ailments, and their outcomes and the seasonal variations; we are not afraid of other complexions, even in cold and moist illnesses. And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
And know, son, that fire cautery is among the essential treatments, and of greater goodness than heated medical cautery.
For fire is simple and does not spread beyond the member that is being cauterized, and does not harm any other member unless it happens to do so.
Heated medicines spread from member to member, causing illnesses that are difficult to heal and potentially killing the patient in some cases.
For fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not cause this, unless there is an excess.
And this I have found through experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is based on the truth of the matter; and for this reason, I excuse myself for the lengthiness of my speech, for I do not wish to deprive you of the secret that lies within fire, and its quality, as well as how it removes illnesses from bodies, just as the philosopher states in his demonstrations. Now receive this in your thoughts.[Comment: This passage suggests that the author is a practitioner who has gained knowledge through experience and study, and he values the effectiveness of fire-based treatments. He wants to share his findings but also preserve their secrecy and the power they hold in healing illnesses.]
And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be performed, and they chose priests.
And I say that a cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm caused by an affliction is reduced by the aid of a cautery; and even when the cautery is necessary to alleviate urgent and severe pain that cannot wait for greater damage to occur to the member.
And never think, dear son, as foolish doctors do; for there is no return of the disease that is healed by cautery; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because a cautery is not just any medicine that changes the complexion, but rather dries up the humors that are the cause of pain, and is valuable for its speed and for the power of its action and authority.
It is possible that the disease sometimes comes according to the complexion of the patient and the location and strength of the disease; and the excesses accumulate in him through the acquisition of food and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in a place where there are few excesses and moisture, such as dens cauteries for pain, and similar things. And this type of pain does not return, but it is rare.
And many people do not understand why cautery is called the "derrière" (hindering) of medicine, and that is true; but they do not believe that cautery can be effective after medical treatment, but their belief is false. The term "cautery is the derrière of medicine" means that when we administer methods of cures for any illness and they are not effective, we then administer cautery, and it is effective. Then it becomes clear that cautery is the "derrière" (hindering) of medicine, but not in the way foolish physicians understand it to be.
The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more effective than iron, and they only claimed this because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance. They also said that the place of cauterization does not become necrotic, but that is not true, as I have experienced. However, I have found that cautery with gold is indeed more effective than iron, just as they claimed.
And yet, when you heat an instrument of gold, you cannot be sure when it is hot enough because of the color of the gold, and it quickly cools down. If it is heated too much, it will become brittle in the fire, which presents a significant challenge.
And so we make use of the fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
I have arranged this chapter on wounds from head to foot, so that the way may be easier to find.
olive cautery
This cautery is good for moistness and coldness in the brain, and there are two that are made for a disease called "soda" (tension headache), and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for an abundance of dreams, pain in the teeth and throat, and also for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis and cramp and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a cleansing medicine, loosening the head three or four nights, depending on what the virtue and the water and the habit of the patient can bear; and then let the patient's head be shaved.
And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on something firm; then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers come, bleed slightly, then heat the cautery called "olivare," of which this is the shape:
And place it on the marked spot with ink, and make a small puncture while pulling downward and outward with your hand; then quickly remove your hand and check the mark to see if you see a small hole; and if you do not see it, reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take a pinch of salt and put it in warm water and soft cotton inside, and place it on the wound, and leave it for three days; then apply a damp cloth soaked in butter and leave it on until the burn is healed; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; and therefore it heals faster.
And some of them said that the cautery should be left on long enough that part of the bone is burned, and then what has been burnt of the bone should be scraped off and treated.[](Note: This treatment may seem barbaric by modern standards. Medical practices in medieval times were often based on superstition and limited knowledge of anatomy and infection. The use of cautery was a common practice, but it could also lead to complications such as infection or excessive scarring.)
And they say that one should leave the cautery for a while, and apply it strongly enough that it leaves a mark as wide as a finger ring that women wear on their thimbles, so that the humors may come out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should clean and suture it.
And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me in every case, except in certain men where there is a dangerous condition; and it seems to me that I should leave the other method; for the head is weakened by continuous loosening through natural means, as we have witnessed in other limbs; and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healthy and effective for me, I use this method to bring about a cure.
of the old pain in the head
When chronic pain comes to the whole head and lasts for a long time, the patient should use herbs and pills which are called "cochie", and purgatives for the head and oils and poultices; and if one applies the cautery as we have said before, but it is not effective.
Take care if the patient's head (chiefly referring to the shoulder area in this medical context) is of strong nature, and that it is not too cold; then cauterize it a little below the fire cautery we mentioned earlier.
Afterward, perform cautery on each horn of the head (referring to the temples) up to the bone, as we mentioned before, and make a "vasel" shaped cautery mark at the spot; it is a blister in which cups are placed. Keep your hand light so that you do not touch the bone. The patient will feel more significant pain in this cautery than in others, but I will speak of that later. It is important that the cauteries on the horns be finer than those used for the middle of the head; this is the method:
of the cautery on the head When there is sudden pain in a part of the head and the illness extends up to the eye, and the head has been purged by cleansing medicines, and other cures as I mentioned in the division of diseases have been attempted without success, then cautery should be performed in two ways: with medication and with fire.
The medical practice of cautery consists of taking a twig of alder, removing the bark and soaking it in a mixture of two parts ground herbs. Then make an incision in the temple where the pain lies, in such a way that the alder twig can be placed under the skin. Once placed, bind and press it tightly for twelve hours, then remove it and leave the wound open for two or three days before applying a compress soaked in butter to promote healing.
After the treatment with ointment has healed, and if you wish to use any of the burning medicines I have written about in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
The iron cautery is done in this manner. Heat the cautery to a degree as shown in the following form:
And it is called "clos" because the tip is shaped like a bell with one small indentation in the middle. Place it on the painful area and hold it there while moving it slightly for a short period of time until half of the tip's thickness has been burnt. Then lift your hand so that the artery, which is located further away from the burn, does not get burned, allowing for an abundant flow of blood to leave the body.[^1^]
Afterward, put cotton in the wound covered with silk, and leave it on for three days; then put wet cotton smeared with butter, and then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this pimple with the cautery called "cultellare," at the whole tip, and be careful not to cover the artery in this pimple which is not old.
of a pimple or swelling.
When you cure a pimple or swelling as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cautery before described with medicine and iron is not enough, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is red; and pass it lightly over the painful place a line of half a finger long, and remove your hand once, and draw back so as not to cover the artery and not reach the bone; and watch out for the jaw that moves when one chews, and the nerve does not move, and that spasms do not come upon the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear, even for those who do not know about it, and who are not trained and experienced; and leave the work half-done; but I will tell you how to stop blood flow when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it fits in this book.
And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is strong, cauterize it in the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.

When pain comes to the ear from coldness, and medical treatments and other cures as we have mentioned in the division have been tried but the pain persists, then heat this "pointed" cautery, of which the form is as follows:
After, point all around the affected ear, or both ears if the pain is in both, and move back a bit from the root of the ear after making a mark; and have ten "points" around each ear; then heal the area until it is healed.[Welcome to the help desk! of the torture of the mouth.
The torture (pain) that should be treated with cautery is only those that are caused by an excess of fluids, as we have mentioned in the divisions of diseases; and do not apply cautery to similar ones that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
When you treat this type of torture that moves with fluid from bodily purges and head cleansings and rinses, and if it is not effective, then you should cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little behind the temple, and the third on the joint of the two lips; place the cautery on the healthy-looking part, and burn the patient near the top of the ear, a little below the ear horn, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery on until half of the heart is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
And the appearance of the knife that we mentioned before is similar, but it is a bit more subtle and requires that the knife be a bit larger; after treating the wound as I have said before, until it heals completely.
When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said before, but it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then perform four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one on the side called "vasselz" as we have mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
The word "litargie" in medieval medical texts usually refers to a type of paralysis or loss of movement in a part of the body, often affecting the face or limbs. It is derived from the Greek word "lethargia," which means "forgetfulness" or "sleepiness." In this context, it likely refers to a condition that causes weakness or numbness, similar to what we now call "lethargy." For this illness, give the patient large quantities of grains and cleansing pills for the brain; then shave the patient's head and apply the plaster of sinapis (mustard seed) to the back of the head, as written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the method of cauterization: perform it as I have said.
If it (the abscess) is cleaned out in this way, that is good; and if not, perform three cauterizations on the head, starting from the crown and going down to the neck, leaving a space of two fingers between each cauterization; and treat it as you would other wounds, and if you see fit and the patient can tolerate it, perform one cauterization in the middle (of the abscess); and if necessary, two others on the two ends (of the abscess), and continue treatment until it is healed; and use the type of cauterization called "olivare," as I have mentioned before.
of the chill/coldness of the head The head must be cleansed with grains and the other things we have mentioned before; then shave the patient's head and perform cauterization on the head and on each horn (temple), and one at the back and three along the spine of the neck; and if necessary, and the body is moist and the patient can tolerate it, and the illness is severe, perform four cauterizations along the spine of the back; and leave it alone until the hottest part of the heat (of the cauterization) has subsided, then remove your hand; then treat it until it is healed, and use the type of cauterization called "olivare," which we have mentioned before.
of epilepsy
Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain of yellowness and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medicine.
And if it is an infant who cannot endure it, have them gargle and chew food that purifies the brain frequently with good meats; then let blood from the middle of the head, and perform one cautery according to what we have said before, and one cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and able to endure it, perform cauteries as I have said for those with paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauteries be olive oil according to the manner that I have said.
If the patient is an infant, perform one subtle cautery according to this method:
When, due to melancholy, superfluities or corrupt moisture cause thick phlegm, then use such hot irons as we have said for someone with paralysis.
And if, due to melancholy, the superfluities tend towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will purify the brain, as mentioned in the previous division.
After that, shave the patient's head; then make a well-made linen compress in the shape of a circle and place it on their head; have the patient lie crosswise and ensure they are well-restrained from all sides; then apply the liniment and warm it with moderately hot fire, so that the heat can be tolerated when applied to the head; then remove the circle from inside the head and let it cool; and do this for the patient once a week with other good treatments until they are healed.
Or, if you wish to cauterize the patient by making multiple punctures with the entire cautery. This method of cauterization moistens the brain excessively; and then place a cotton pad soaked in butter and gelatin on top.
of the eyelid(s) When the eyelid swells for the first time with the signs that I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink something cleansing for the head and guarding against all moistures, and make him sweat or take baths several times while fasting.
After that, order the patient to tilt their head back, and perform cautery in the middle of the forehead, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the swelling of the eyelid is on both eyes together, or on one if it is only on one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are under the skin for the entire length of the cautery, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and watch for blood flow, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it as well as you can.
And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in making incisions, how to stop them with caution; and sometimes cautery or a hot iron is done under the two bones at the back.
of the body of tears
When the tears from the eyes are old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are apparent on the outside of the head; and it is seen that these are cold fluids of phlegm, then perform the cautery that I have said at the beginning of the eye treatment: one cautery in the middle of the forehead, two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries in the hollows below the two bones; and if more is needed, cauterize it profusely above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
within the body of tears inside the eyes
When you treat the patient according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the sick person three roasted chickpeas to drink; after that, apply a cautery to the middle of the head with an olive-shaped cautery; and make two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the eyebrows, slightly below the hair; and be careful not to cover the artery. And this is the shape of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
When the paper of the eye has been softened by disease and moisture, then use this cautery, which is called "olivary," of which the following is the form:
And if you wish to do so, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the eyebrows are; and do not remove your hand until a third part of the paper has been burned, according to the method that I have described.
the hair that points to the eye It sometimes happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and then cauteries are made in two ways: either by fire or by a burning medicine.
For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the eyelashes grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so that they do not move until they grow.
When they are born and even, then place the patient in your care; afterward, on a piece of paper place an image that is similar to the leaf of a fern, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and pearl powder on the eye, then heat the cautery to the shape described here:
After cauterizing near the mark that you have made many times, so that the skin is burnt there; and the sign of a successful procedure is seeing the paper retracted and the hairs standing up at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like that for three days. Then apply moist cotton until the burn is healed; after that, treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
And if after that the hairs return and the paper becomes softened, then reapply the cautery to the same spot as before, just as you did at first; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper rises up to its natural position, and is even, and do not cause any pain to the eye.
The fiery medical cautery is what you should instruct the patient to do, letting their hairs grow long and even until they are full-grown; then make a form from parchment in the shape of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them together well; and work quickly so that it does not cool down. Spread this mixture on the form as if it were a fern leaf, and place it on the paper over the eyes. If the illness affects only one eye, then you should work on just one, and if in both eyes, do the same; and place moist cotton beneath the affected eye, using egg white. The patient's head should be in your care, and place your hand over the medicine, pressing once every time the patient feels a burning sensation from the medicine, for they will feel it as if it were fire. When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from its case. And when the biting (insect) has passed, lift the cloth and check if you see the skin stretched as if it had been stretched by heat or incision; and if it is so, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine to the cloth until your work is even and your eyes are healed; then place a wet cotton compress soaked in butter over the burnt area until the burn has cooled down. Afterwards, cure the wound dressing called "dyafenis" and others until it is healed.
And if you need to be careful with your work and ensure that no medicine drips into the eyes. And if the skin becomes soft, and hairs prick the eye, then reapply the medicine to the affected area where the skin has softened, just as you did before; after that, cure it until it is healed. This is the method for treating an inflamed eye:
And know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this should be your constraints; and do not apply the same treatment to everyone, as the study of this art requires.
of the treatment of fistula by cautery
When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on them in this manner.
Command the patient to place their head in your lap; and have the assistant hold the patient's head between your hands so that it does not move or deviate; then apply a cotton swab soaked with egg white or parsley juice on the eye; then heat up the cautery tool which is parted: and attach it to the head so that it forms like the shape of a dove's feather quill, bring the two ends together so that they meet, and if you wish, sharpen it from one end to the other, and if you wish, make it curved like a tent; but in any case, this tool is useful for your work.
Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and extract the rotten tissue and pus from it; and if it is closed, incise it and extract the contents; then place hot bran on top of the cautery tool, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part above the eye so that your hand does not move excessively; and apply the cautery to the fatty tissue of the eyelid and corrupt it.
If you come to the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, it would be good. If not, then perform cautery again and as many times as necessary, leaving it for three days; then place a cotton swab soaked in butter on top of it, and treat the inflammation until it is healed; and if 40 days have passed and it has not yet healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and refer to what comes next in the chapter.
And there is a kind of fire cautery for fistula that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "fistula," and break the opening; then place in the split a thin probe of such material as follows: And they make it to the quantity of a thumb's width; and hold your hand firmly on the probe, ensuring that the patient does not move at all, lest the melted lead flows into their eye; and it is necessary to place over the patient's eye a piece of damp cotton soaked in egg white or oil: the lead will draw out the pus from the fistula with marvelous healing.
And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have mentioned, that is good. If not, one must administer a puncture to the abscess and return the fistula to the body of the abscess as appropriate in its specific location.
of ruptures on the lips Many times, cracks appear on lips that are called "wrinkles," and similarly on children's lips.
When you treat these cracks as we have mentioned in divisions, and the treatment does not work, then heat a small scalpel-shaped fire cautery of this shape:
And quickly place it in the cracks until it reaches the root; after, cure the wound with a cerate until it is healed.
of the abscess of the throat
When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has rotted and burst and become a fistula; and you treat it as we have mentioned in divisions, but it does not improve: then you need to use a cautery according to the size of the fistula; place the probe or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and behind the opening; and do this once or twice, after treating it as we have mentioned in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is treated this way, it is good; but if not, then you must uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, as you will find it in its chapter.[Note: The original text uses "cautere" which means a hot iron or scalpel, while the term "fer chaud" in the translated text means "hot iron". Also, the translation of "enveillis" is changed to "burst" from "festered" for better understanding.]
from movement of the teeth
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines but it is of no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery so that its shape will be as described later, with a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cautery according to your desire; afterwards, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water and hold it for an hour and then spit it out.
And in this manner, the moving tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the moisture is corrupted and dried up.
of tooth pain
When tooth pain comes from coldness, whether it is real or imagined, and medical treatments are not effective, then it is necessary to use the cautery in two ways: with butter cautery and fire cautery.[ next line ]
Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, and soak it in boiled butter, and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it there until it cools down; and do this often until the virtue of the butter reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see it necessary, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the tip of the tooth.
The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, from which the shape will come after, and place it on the tooth while holding your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, for the pain will be relieved on the same day or the next. And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in preparation for this cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the shape of the cautery:
When the scrofulous swellings are due to phlegm and cold moistures, and are not responsive to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire-steel so as to produce the following form, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the side away from the cautery; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice, as needed, until it reaches the base of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply a cautery in proportion to its size, and leave it on for three days; then apply a wet cotton compress soaked in butter until the burn is healed; after that, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.

of the pleurisy cautery

of the fleshy part which is called "thigh"
When you cut the thigh, heat the fire-brand that looks like a razor, and then place it all glowing hot on the cut thigh; leave your hand there until the brand reaches the base of the vein, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of flesh, cauterize each part as we have said; after that, use wound-healing treatments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large fire-brand made of alum, it will be of greater help.
of an improperly treated wound
When the patient cannot tolerate surgery or incision (which we will discuss later), then there comes a disease that can only be healed by cauterization.
When a fistula comes to someone, and it is mature and casts rottenness and corrupt humors, you should test it with a thin probe, and make sure that you know the depth of the probe entirely. Afterwards, heat the cautery which looks like a razor, and put it into the fistula according to the quantity that the probe has entered, and reheat the cautery until the rotten and corrupt flesh is burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of flesh needing to be removed; and take care not to burn the nerves which are inside, and the large veins. If the fistula goes to the body of the bladder and the intestines, beware of these areas, and do not make cuts outside of the fleshy area, and consider that it is not persistent; after healing the area until it is healed, and if the area protrudes, and the contents are removed for a long time, then know that the area is fully healed; and if the contents are not removed, know that the area is full, and the bone at the base is rotten; and thus one of these as we shall say in its place.

When humorous vapors descend to the joint of the hip, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and one sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the place of separation is clearly visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip bone with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark before the separation around the joint as it turns, so that the hip bone is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used for stomach cauterization.

for hip pain When pain comes to the joint of the hip, and it is caused by coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated for this as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of heavy humors with stinking pills, or other good similar ones.
Afterward, perform cauterization; and the methods of cauterization are of two kinds: that is to say, hot medicinal irons, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is of many kinds, one of which is as follows: you cauterize on the joint of the swelling three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make a deep and large wound between each cautery the width of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a single cautery is done in the middle on top of the swelling, so that there are four in total according to this form:
And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we previously mentioned for the dislocation of the swelling; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire swelling, and all the flesh around the edge is burned.
And this is the method used in sciatica, when the pain is located in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg. If it reaches the thigh and the leg, then two cauteries are done where the patient indicates that the pain is, and one circular cautery above the ankle four fingers wide, slightly to the left; and let the cauteries be of a knife-like shape, and let the flesh around the edge be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends down to the bones of the foot or near it, then cauterize there where they feel the pain three or four times with the pointed cautery that is called "points".
And if necessary, more are done; and if they know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then a knife-like or circular cautery is done, and be careful in all your cauteries to not leave the cautery on for so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
And I myself have seen several who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled up completely, and the foot as well, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted. Afterwards, they died from a stomach ailment.
And if the pain is in two places together, perform cautery on both, following this method. // And the wise men said in the cautery for inflammation, of which this is the method, make a iron that is as thick as a thumb's width of dactyl (a unit of measurement), or just a bit less, and it should be interlaced, and let there be a space between the interlacings equal to the size of a nut; and let the interlacings be turned two ways, and let them be like knots, and let there be one handle of iron well-made; and this is its shape.
And heat it until it is completely red and starts to drip, then place it on the swollen boil of the patient, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one application of the iron, leaving it for three days; then apply a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) said that we use little of this cautery due to fear of its appearance, and there are few who use it; but it is one of the good cauteries for those who can tolerate it, and where it is applied.[IMPRESSION]
of the pain of the back
When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or being struck, or from excessive bleeding, or from the spreading of cold matter, none of these instances is appropriate for cauterization, except in the case of one caused by the infusion of cold matter.
It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with foul-smelling pills or similar treatments, three lines be signed on the back, in the area where the pain is located, using incense; and within each line, five cauterizations or more should be made, depending on the strength and quantity that the patient can tolerate; and let the cauterization be done using the type of cauterization called "poins"; and if you wish, make three or four cauterizations using the clavile moien technique, in this form:
This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have stiff necks when they get up, and fear; and you will find on the last spine in the back, and the appearance which comes above the other spines.
When you see these signs and wish to cure them, cauterize with the cautery of this type, in this form:
So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine equally. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine using the cautery, making two or three lines, and have the points close to one another. Afterwards heal the area until it is healed, as we have said, and beware not to apply cautery to gout that is in a nerve spasm.
of joint pain
When joint pain is due to moisture spread throughout the entire body, and when it occurs in the feet, which is called "gout" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it can be treated with cautery in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let them be olive-shaped, as follows:
And if necessary, make the cautery on the sole of the foot with the entire surface of the cauterizing instrument, which is called "point." And if the pains come up to the knee and other joints, which happens often, make three or four cauteries on each knee, in every part, with the entire olive-shaped cautery; and if you need more, do so, but do not keep your hand there for too long that the thickness of the skin is burned.
And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines long; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and have them take medicines. For if you take good care of them and purge fluids, they will be healed with the help of God.
Of the opening of the abscess.
When the abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see to cure it, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that empty the belly, so that the feces descend from their belly; after make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has receded, and press gently with your fingers around the abscess on the bone of the wrist, and make a sign like half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: [Here a picture/diagram would follow in the original text]
...until it is white and exudes pus. And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your efforts are in vain. And it is necessary for the cauteries of children to be fine according to the measure of eggs, and also for adults as large according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is removed; after curing other remedies until it is healed, and let the patient lie down for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time, so that the bubbles do not burst when he gets up in chambers.
And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him and carry it for another forty days; and have good rest, that he moves little and guards against excessive consumption of drink and food, and loud talking; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. of old pain in some member When pain comes to a member because of a fall or injury and that pain lasts for a long time and medical treatment is ineffective, then it is necessary that the area be cauterized with the "point" cautery, and let the cautery match the length of the member, its size, weakness, and power, as well as its location and level of pain. If the wound heals from the first cautery, that's good; if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for sometimes it is necessary to change the location of the cautery on the body part, therefore one must perform cauteries until the patient heals.
of leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and also the diseases that come from the putrefaction of humours and melancholy. When you see a patient to be cauterized, pay attention if the disease is at its beginning and if it has been treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not worsen or linger, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the body, then perform five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the forehead, another towards the front at the end of the hairline; and two on the temples, and one at the back near the nape; and leave your hand there long enough for the cautery to reach the bone, and until the scabs come out, so that the vapors of the foul humours can escape; and cauterize on the skin according to what it looks like before.
And if the diseased place is spread out everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the following cauteries that we have mentioned in the head: one cautery on the nose, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large one on the hip and another next to it, two on the shoulders, two on the elbows, two on the knees of the legs, one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are at the back of the heel so as not to burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
Know that the more you do cautery, the more help you provide and the more it benefits the patient; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because the body is already corrupt. And you should make the cautery big or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the ways of irons. After the cure, dust the wound with flour of vetch and honey and other cures until it is healed.
"of inflammation" or "swelling"
When swelling comes to any limb and is treated by medicines, oils, and plasters, yet it is not healed, then cautery is done on the limb according to the size of the member; and let the cautery be a little deep in the flesh; then cure it with dressings until it is healed. And sometimes cautery is done on the hand, foot, and back, at the opening of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should intervene if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the openings of the nerves moving the body.

When the disease called "albaras" has become advanced and the means of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the size of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and the color changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of a rooster and pigeon, each in equal parts; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
The treatment of cancer (or more accurately, "chancre") by cautery refers to the use of hot metal instruments to burn or destroy diseased tissue. This was a common medical practice in medieval times due to the lack of effective surgical techniques and anesthetics. Here's a possible line-by-line translation:
When a chancre begins and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre. And yet, wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, using the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
of the swelling that cannot grow
When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays in growing or due to the excess fluid it makes, or due to the water of the patient if they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its growth: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries by pricking; then leave it like that. Because it will hasten to die.
And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery like this: (followed by a description of shaping the cautery)
And place your hand in the middle of the ailment called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the core, and such that the cauteries are felt from outside in such a way that the course of the rotting is eased. Afterward, cure it until it is perfectly healed.
the cure of fire by iron
There is another kind of disease called "corrodens," which is nothing but an eating away of the member, for it consumes the members just like fire consumes dry wood. If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate cautery along with fire, then heat the cauteries, small and large, according to what is appropriate for the place where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing remain of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it alone for three days, and put on poultices with oil on the cauterized places until the burns from the fire are healed, and all of the corruption. Afterward, cure it with ointments that generate flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh is not born, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places. And this eating away has sometimes been cured by medicinal agents instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater aid, and I have already said the cure for medicinal agents in the division: take them when you need them.
of the corns that come to the feet
Often happens that in the feet a sickness is born which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large abscessed thing that wounds the foot. And the cauteries for this sickness are of two kinds. That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is when you heat up a probe-like lancet as big as a roof beam, made of good iron, measured so it can touch the nail from all sides, and having sharp edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until you reach the base of the nail; and leave it like that for three days until it begins to rot; then apply a plaster of crushed marsh mallow with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the wound with a cleansing ointment until it is healed.
And if they are converted by moisture in the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this way: take a rod of iron or copper, or a probe-like lancet, and place it on the nail and the stylet, that is to say, porrelly verrucae; and place the rod on top so that it heats up all around, then add some hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edges of the rod come to the root of the nail, and can find a deep path through the hot water to the root; and have the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will uproot all its roots. Do this one after another, until you reach all those in the body, then cure the wounds with cleansing ointments that cause flesh to grow.
I would translate "li cure dou trembler" as "the treatment for trembling".
When some people tremble from cold nerves or quartan fever or other causes, then you should make four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one in the foot, and one on the stomach at the olive cautionery; this will stop the trembling, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
of smelly pustules
Sometimes appear on the body, due to a lack of bathing, or smelly pustules that come from corrupt matter. It is necessary, when they first appear, to apply cautery to each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made of myrtle wood, with its tip taken by fire, or of long aristolochia root, or of the lenticular cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but rather the excess is broken up from which they come, and they heal; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
when an artery is cut It often happens that there is great loss of blood from the artery which is cut in the wound, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop [the bleeding].
And yet, when this happens to someone, hurry to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more drips from it; then heat various olive-shaped cauteries, both large and small, until they are all red; then take one, whether large or small, according to the size and location of the wound in which the artery is cut, and place the cautery on this vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.
And if it jumps out when you lift your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take another one quickly from the fire.
And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and take care not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood runs from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially if the artery is large, unless it is through one of the four ways that we have said: through cauterization, or through extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and constricted appropriately.
One who will administer stopping the bleeding by tightly binding with bandages or placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not help much.[Original text is in Medieval French, and I am providing a translation into Modern English.]
And if this happens to someone who does not have any remedy or medicine present, then they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it stops bleeding over the wound and over the vein; and they must not move it, but moisten it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations for what they need in terms of cautery and medicines.
We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and described the operations, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have placed the chapter on fevers from head to foot, and I will go in this chapter along the same path so that one may more easily find what one wants.
And so, as I begin this one, it is important, dear son, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
And I warn you not to undertake foolish things. For many kinds of people come to be cured, some of whom are so afflicted with their illness that they easily die due to the severity and greatness of its malice; and one should fear for these. And of these, there are some who claim to be healed and say: "wait, I am healed"; and the illness is deceitful. It is not at all appropriate for you to agree with those who come to you with this attitude, but rather put more effort into your honor than into your greed. Do not rashly but wisely open up those from whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain benefit and praise; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients for their health to be restored; and this will help you to establish a good reputation, and glory, and memories of praise.

a swollen head filled with water.

tears

of the stopping of the ears
All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: either grains, or animals, or mineral stones such as iron; or seeds, such as lice, beans, peas; or fluids such as water and ashes and similar things.
When something falls into the ear, such as a stone or other object that does not stick to or grow in the ear, place the ear in the sun. If it comes out using pincers, that is good; if not, then facilitate extraction using a thin probe wire of fine double-wire. And if it does not come out using any of the things we have mentioned, then hurry to lance the ear so that abscess and hardening may occur, as well as spasm; and the manner of lancing is such that you should first bleed the patient from the cephalic vein, and draw blood according to their strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty tissue or flesh; and let the incision be like a crescent moon, coming to the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck it out with your mouth; and continue the treatment until it is healed. "de l'estoupement des oreilles" means "on ear stoppers/plugs". The term refers to the act of blocking or stopping up the ears, typically by inserting a piece of cotton or other material to prevent air or fluid from entering or escaping. This technique can be used for various purposes, such as protecting the ears during bathing, diving, or flying, relieving ear pain due to changes in pressure, or preventing water from entering the ear canal and causing infection. In a medieval medical context, ear stoppers could also be used in conjunction with distillations or other treatments for the ears.

The one then that goes deep, if it cannot be seen, is of difficult healing in many cases, and in the one that can be seen, it is necessary that you expose the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the blockage apparent, work on it immediately with this tool, as described in the following form:
And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind, so that it does not wound the ear; if the blockage is from pus or flesh in the ear, hold it with fine forceps and gently scrape it until all the flesh is removed.
And if the blockage is deep in the ear, take a fine, light razor, heat it slightly over fire, and then place it on the flesh of the ear. If you feel the blockage, and the patient feels pain when hearing, make a small incision carefully, being careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then insert a wick in the ear according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Do this for some days until the wound is healed, or take a tent and soak it in rose water, and powder on top of vitriol broken; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary that you draw the tent and apply another tent soaked in cerote made of oil rose and wax, as long as the swelling is gone; then cure it until it is healed.

"of the hairs of papers"
When hairs grow on papers that are not natural and are old, they harm the eyes and cause various kinds of illnesses such as excessive tearing, softening of the eyelids, and inflammation, to the point that it can lead to eye destruction. of eye ulcers (or: of eye rottenness)
When this disease called "aleacrati" or ulceration occurs in the eye, it can happen in two ways: naturally and unnaturally. It can occur suddenly due to a wound, a cut, or cauterization, and through similar things.
And the manner of the treatment is that you split that suture, and separate its lips, and put linen bandages inside, and bind it until it is healed; and it is not at all appropriate to use drying and constricting substances in the cure of it. And the treasure of your cure is that you take care that it does not heal in the same shape as it was before; and this work that we have mentioned is only a remedy for this disease, so that it does not return to its former shape.

of the flesh that grows above the pupil
Sometimes a red flesh is born in men's eyes, covering the pupil and pressing on the membranes, turning them outwards, appearing like a rose of baluster; and the procedure is that the patient places his head over your sanction, then you open their eyes, and pull all that flesh with suitable tweezers, holding it tight; then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting to the end, but be careful not to wound the eye during the process; and let the incision be made with a scalpel as we mentioned in the incision of the nail and small splinters that are removed, just as the form shows after this chapter.

of the eye socket.

of the flesh above the nostrils
Sometimes diverse fleshy growths are born on or near the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such growths that have a swollen flesh of fox color, and others have soft flesh of good color. of flesh from (the) nose

to cut the tie of the tongue.
Sometimes there is a tie under the tongue that is natural and present at birth, or it can occur due to an accidental closing of a wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your hands, then lift the tongue and cut the nervous band that holds it in place with a large enough incision so that the tongue is loosened from its support. And if there is toughness or knots, which comes from sudden wound closing, use a hook to cut this connective tissue. Be careful not to make the incision too deep, as the artery is located beneath it. Once you have done this, rinse the area with rose water and/or warm or cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue. The patient should use it every night to prevent reconnection. If bleeding occurs, apply vitriol powder to the wound, and if the bleeding persists, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose. Then continue treatment until it heals.

I treated a woman for an abscess in her throat, which was quite large and obstructing her windpipe, such that the woman could not exhale through the passage that was blocked and could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had stayed like that for one day or two. And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced two teeth out of her nostrils. I hurried then and inserted a probe into one of the nostrils, extracted pus, and drained a lot of matter; then I did the same in the other nostril and opened her mouth while pressing on her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut out some of it, and only a little blood came out; and so, the blocked passage of the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut the abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing and filling up the space that I had emptied, becoming very large; so I performed surgery on it and cauterized it inside her throat: this stopped its growth, and I left. And I do not know what God did with her after me.

The chapter of abscesses.
Many similarities of abscess exist, according to what memory brings forth hereafter, one and the other in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is in two ways: one is in its own likeness, and those that hold moisture. And the second manner is according to their locations in the body. For the abscess of the head is different than that of the base, and the abscess of the fleshy part is different than that which comes in joints, and each one has its own judgment in the work.
And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its completion; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is completely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have become corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the base, so one should pierce it when it is dead; and one must not pierce a grown abscess without completion of digestion, except for that which is near the base, lest it rot inwardly and become elongated, forming a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is mature according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the lessening of the fever, and the diminishing of the pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the place where it is most dependent on the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and at nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no crease.
And in those that crease, according to the member. And when abscess is in fleshy parts, it is better to leave the incision until it has strengthened after completion of digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body's fluid will be elongated and full of much filth; and perhaps the edges and the depths become hardened. And there are some abscesses that must be pierced according to the width of the body, according to what is necessary for the member. And one must enlarge in small abscesses with small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses that require cutting out the core and covering it; when it has become as one cloth and is dead, it must be done as with boils: and there are some that are cut in three angles, and some that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of glands; and some that require a round cut, and other cuts and similar cutting out.
Those who have no visible swelling, such as a soft abscess, you should fully pierce; and when the abscess is large, and has collected pus, you should not pull out all the pus in that hour, but only a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw out some more; do this many times, gradually, until all the pus comes out; do the same even if the patient is of weak vitality, such as women, small children, old and frail men. For the spirit sometimes jumps at the moment of pus expulsion, which may cause the death of the patient, and you would not notice. Therefore, be very cautious in this matter, and when you have pierced your abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a clean cut, then apply linen or old cotton bandages; but if it is large abscesses with many holes, then you should put in a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have cut off a piece of skin from the abscess and turned it over, then you should fill it with old linen rags or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and dress the wound until it is healed.
And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and a wet cloth to the area multiple times. If the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is during winter, and the place where the abscess is located is very sensitive, then you should put tents and wet cloths soaked in warm wine and oil on it; and if it is in the summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should apply cloths soaked in water and oil, or wine and cold oil, until the third day as we have said; and then unbind the abscess and wipe it and dress it, as appropriate, until it is healed.
And this is what must be universally understood in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.

The term "scrophules" refers to a type of abscess or swollen lymph node, typically found in the neck. The name comes from the Greek word "skirphere", meaning "hard tubercle". Scrofula is often associated with tuberculosis infection and was commonly referred to as the "King's Evil" in medieval Europe, where it was believed that the touch of a monarch could cure the disease. However, this belief has been proven to be false and scrofula is now treated with antibiotics and other medical interventions.
"Scrophules" often appear in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes occur elsewhere on the body, and are multiple, adhering to one another.
