of the chancre
We have said in the division the similarities of chancre and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre worsens in the groin, and great caution is needed in the cure. And the ancients said that when chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as chancre which is on the breasts, and on the thigh, and in similar places, it should all be removed when it starts; and when it is large and old, one must not approach it, for I never cured anyone of it before, nor did anyone ever cure it before me.
And the operation, when it is in a location where it can be removed, as we have said, involves purging the patient of black bile once; then make them bleed if they show clear signs of congestion; then prepare the patient for the procedure by having them empty their bowels. Then cast your leeches or cupping glasses on the chancre and remove all hairs from around it, leaving nothing behind. Allow the blood to flow freely, and carefully clean the area with your hand or some other object. If the bleeding opposes the incision of an artery or vein, cauterize the area until the bleeding stops. Then continue with another treatment until the wound heals.
of dropsy We have previously said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and how the gathering of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: only mentioning; and one should not touch the iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and hydrops ascites, for it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy which is called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, look to see if the patient is weak, or if they have another illness besides dropsy, such as pleurisy and loosening of the bowels and similar things; then do not touch it with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of strong constitution, and they have no illness other than dropsy alone, and they are neither too young nor too old, then one should proceed thus: Lay the patient flat on your hands, and have the assistant press the belly by pushing the water towards the lowest part of the bladder, then take the pointed spatula according to this form: And let it be sharpened in two parts to a point, but yet not so sharp that it can reach the intestines when inserted, and let it not be able to cut;
Then, look to see if the dropsy has spread towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision above the belly button three fingers wide and straight down to the poignil; and if the dropsy is due to illness of the liver, let your incision be on the left side of the belly button three fingers wide; and if it is due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is important that the patient does not lie on the incision so that the superfluidities do not run to this weak place;
Then, puncture all the skin with the instrument, and lift it up, and place your hand on the spatula between the skin and the abscess as in flaying to the width of a fingernail or thereabouts; then puncture the abscess until the spatula reaches the cavity, and this is the location of the water, then pull it out, and insert this instrument of which this is the form: And it is similar to a silver awl, and is made of light bronze or iron, and has in its lower part one small hole; and on one side, three holes; and two on another, and one on another; and the edges are sharpened like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision that writers make the quill:
upon the head is the humeral bone, so that when the instrument touches the water, it immediately sinks down onto the instrument; then empty half or a third of it, because if you empty more than necessary at that hour, it may happen that the patient dies due to the resolution of his spirit by the weapon, or he falls unconscious, or he approaches death.
but empty it according to the amount of its strength, and according to what the vital signs of the patient indicate, and his pulses; then pull the instrument out and hold the water, which is now retained by the pressure that stops up the opening above the syphac, as I have mentioned, which you pierce in this manner; then reinsert the instrument the next day if you see the patient tolerating it, and withdraw a small amount of water.
do this every day, and be careful not to withdraw too much water until only a little remains. And if you are uncertain about the patient, and leave too much water, cure them with burial or hot sand, and by sweating or bathing in the sun, and staining them with wine; and use drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
of the blocking of the penis. Sometimes a child is born who has no opening in the penis, or the opening is small or not in its proper place. In such cases, it is necessary to make a tiny incision of one spatulam (a unit of measurement) with a very fine awl following this form: then insert a fine plug of linen cloth into the opening and keep it in place for three or four days. When he wishes to urinate, remove the plug and allow him to pass urine, and then replace the plug. It may happen that it is not necessary to replace the plug, as the urine that comes out will not close the opening. The one whose opening is small can be treated with a linen cloth plug as we have said, and it will widen. Those who do not have an opening in the proper place are injured, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, which makes them unable to urinate unless they raise their penis; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the urethra, and this is a bad condition.
And the method of the procedure is as follows: have the patient lie down on his back, then stretch out the penis and hold it in a way that the opening is in the middle, like the width of a pen, as it should be. Be careful to avoid any bleeding, which can occur frequently. If it does happen, stop the bleeding using a styptic, and continue treating the wound until it heals.
pustules on the penis Many times these ulcers occur on the penis, and it is a nasty appearance of flesh; and there are malignant and benign ones; so one should take them with a subtle incision, and cut and clean all (of it), then put wet cotton with Egyptian ointment on it; then cure it with definitive ointment until it is healed. And if the ulcer is malignant, with a foul color and discharge, then one should apply cautery to it. When you have cut it out, and if the ulcer is in the root of the penis, and has part inside the skin and part outside, then one must remove the ulcer that is inside first; and when it is healed, then cure the outside part. Because when you cure it all at once, the head of the penis is not assured that it will not be pierced, and there will come blackness and corruption in its penis and anus; so one must cut out everything that is black and corrupted, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate rinds and vinegar, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
And if bleeding occurs, then apply the lunar cautery in this manner: The cautery is helpful for two conditions together: that is, for bleeding and corruption; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, then one must insert a reed of plumbers' wax and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin at the tip of the penis, which happens to those who have not been circumcised, or it happens due to wound or abscess, becomes dry, then one must scrape it with a small instrument until the foreskin is loosened, and the head of the penis is freed from all sides.
And if this is difficult to discuss, then one must scrape it with a spatula a little at the tip of the penis and the skin; then carefully separate between two (parts), and put a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water, which does not become dry again.
of circumcision
Circumcision is not the same as the loosening of continuity like other wounds; nonetheless, when we perform this work willingly, and specifically on children, it is necessary that we do the best and easiest work for their health.
I say that the ancients did not mention circumcision of their children, for they did not practice it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.[I would like to see a translation of this text from Old French into English:
Because I have seen that the majority of masters and healers who perform circumcision do so within a day after birth, and with forceps and a single scalpel; they avoid cutting too deep because there are two layers there, and by chance one may cut the upper layer and leave the lower one.
Or the result is that they cut too deep and the pain is doubled, and at the time of cleansing which takes place on the eighth day, the tip of the member is not necessarily healed; and during the cleansing of the nail, by chance the iron may slip and ruin the work, and this happens many times so that it is not necessary to cleanse and I have seen it.
Of the suturing that is done with thread to the entire wound I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the sutures cut precisely both above and below.
For when you press your hand, you cut evenly in one continuous motion; but the thread must be tightly wrapped around the skin; and the manner of the first work is such that you make the child think, if they pay attention, that you are only tying the thread around the rod, and then afterwards you delight them in all ways possible. Then hold the rod straight between your hands or under your feet so that the child cannot see it or any of the instruments; then place your hand on the rod and blow or cough, and pull upwards until the glans of the rod is exposed; then clean it well of any impurities that have gathered, then tie a double thread signet around the base, then tie another thread to it; and hold it with two fingers by the second knot at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two knots, then quickly lift the glans and pull the foreskin of the rod.
Then hold the rod straight between your hands or under your feet so that the child cannot see it or any of the instruments; then place your hand on the rod and blow or cough, and pull upwards until the glans of the rod is exposed; then clean it well of any impurities that have gathered, then tie a double thread signet around the base, then tie another thread to it; and hold it with two fingers by the second knot at the thumb and index finger, and cut between the two knots, then quickly lift the glans and pull the foreskin of the rod. Let the blood flow a little, for this is beneficial; then put powder on it repeatedly, and on top of that place a cloth dampened with a half of an egg cooked and mixed with rosewater, combined with good and fresh rose oil, and leave it on until the next day and treat it with other treatments until it heals.
The procedure for purging is as follows: let the two ends be even and sharp, and let them be of equal length as the width of the hand.
The error in purging is when the heart exits through the incision; then you must stretch it to your fingernail, so that the wound forms an abscess; and cut it evenly, and if you cannot hold it at your fingernail, hold it with pincers, and then cut.
And if three days have passed and what is beneath the penis is swollen, then leave it alone until the abscess has subsided, and gently flay it; cut it as much as you can move it, and be careful near the part of the penis, it will not harm anything.[*Note: I am assuming "verge" here refers to the penis due to the context. However, this word can also mean "rod" or "stick" in Old French.*]
Then cure the wound with powder, as we have said in the treatise on powders, and if you cut too deeply into the heart and it goes beyond, it will not harm; therefore cure it as we have said until it is healed.
concerning the retention of urine
The retention of urine is due to blockage by a kidney stone, or coagulated blood, or pus, or feces, or similar things, as mentioned in the division (classification).
And if the urine is not released and you see that the retention is due to a stone located in the bladder or urethra, then the patient should be placed on their knees, with their feet on their back, stretching their belly over the back, and pulling the patient's abdomen as much as they can. This will put pressure on the bladder neck causing the stone to pass and the urine to flow.
If it does not come out as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should use an instrument called a "syringe" to extract it. Here is its shape: it should be made of thin silver, lightweight, similar to the feathers of a bird; with a handle one and a half palms long, and fine at the tip.
The method of releasing the urine is as follows: take a double thread and tie a piece of wool or cotton to its tip, insert the tip of the thread into the syringe, cut off excess wool, and push it up to the tip of the syringe. Then apply oil or butter and egg yolk on the syringe, make the patient sit on a chair, anoint the bladder and penis with moist oil, olive oil and warm water;
then gently insert the syringe into the member, until it reaches the base of the member, then bend the member upwards towards the belly; then push the syringe forward until it reaches the bladder, and let the patient feel it reach the empty place, and this is not done in any other order except that the conduit through which it passes may be twisted; then stretch the string along the entire length of the wool yarn, and the urine will follow the wool, then pull it out, and let the urine flow.
and repeat the process of inserting the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and let the patient be relieved.
of bladder diseases.
When ulcers or blood come into the bladder, or there is putrefaction gathered, and you wish to distill waters and medicines into it, then make use of an instrument called a "clepsydra," and this is its form:
It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the place where the medicinal plug should be, such that it stops the member well without addition, if one can draw out the moisture, and push in when necessary.
And when you see to insert your medicines into the bladder, put the tip of the instrument into the moisture, and pull the train that is on it; by doing so, you will draw the moisture to the instrument, and then strongly push the train back in; this way, the moisture will enter in, and come to the bladder now, such that the patient will feel it.
And this is the form of the subtle enema with which one administers an enema to the bladder; it is as follows:
And it is made of silver or brass, and the tip is raised up; and beneath there is a loop where the string hangs down; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in it that you wish to administer to the bladder, then tie it tightly between the two breasts with a good strong doubled thread, and heat one quart of this moisture over the fire; then insert the tip of the enema into the member, and press your hand on the bladder until all of the moisture has entered, such that the patient feels that this moisture has now come to the bladder.
And if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle out of it, and pierce it evenly; then put a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle like you would a bucket, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and tie it to the instrument; and do the same as you did with the bladder, of pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
of the stone.
We have already mentioned in the division the types of stones and their extraction methods along with medicines; and I have told you the difference between the moved stone in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you clearly and concisely.
I say that the stone which is moved in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and it appears sandy, and the patient urinates frequently, and then constricts; and there are many of these jumps in the foundation; and the healing is light in children until they reach 4 years old, and is very difficult in the elderly, and is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
And when we come to the cure, it is necessary to first cleanse the patient through an enema, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines. For it sometimes hinders the search for the stone.
Then take the patient by the feet and straighten them out, and move him downward, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and comes out at times; then make him sit between your prepared hands, and let his hands be beneath his thighs, so that the bladder is completely tilted downwards; then search for it and touch it from inside.
If you feel the stone in the space, then hurry to cut into the stone. And if it does not fall at the touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is old, or your middle finger if the patient is a fully grown young adult; and insert it into his bottom, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it towards the neck of the bladder; then press on it with your finger, and push it out where you intend to cut.
And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to lift up the patient's hips with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the hips in the area where the incision will be made; then insert the spatula, which is its shape:[img width=500]https://i.imgur.com/X3Rn6MH.png[/img] (Note: The image shows a modern medical tool called a "vaginal speculum", but it gives an idea of what a "spatula" might have looked like in the medieval period.)
And make an incision between what is between the haunches and the buttocks, not in the middle but next to the left thigh; and let it be straight on the stone, and your hands should be placed either above the buttocks or below, and let the cutting tool be of a size that it is wide in front, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large.
Perhaps the pressure from the hands on the buttocks will cause it to come out easily without effort; and know that there are some stones that have angles and edges, and they are difficult to extract; and there are some that are soft, similar to a hailstone, round, for which the extraction is easy.
For those stones that have angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out easily, you must use pincers that are like a file at the tip to firmly pull the stone so that it does not break; or place a thin curved instrument underneath it; and if you cannot manipulate it in this way, widen the opening slightly and if the flesh is cut, tighten it with vitriol.
And if there is more than one stone, first place the largest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut above it and pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several. And if it is very large, it must be smoothed and a larger wound must be made. Because two things can happen to the patient: either they die, or urine constantly comes out through the opening so that the wound cannot heal; but still try to pull it out or break it apart with pincers as much as you can until you extract it in pieces.
And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place a damp cloth on it soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then turn the patient towards his collarbone and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
And when you unbind it, rinse the wound well with a mixture of oil and water, then apply a dressing of fine-ointment and basilic ointment until it is healed.
And if hot abscesses or corrosions come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained in such a way that it comes out drop by drop: then put your finger into the wound and draw out the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to rot.
Then raise the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and help it in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat it, you bind the patient's two thighs together and apply the medicine to the wound.
And if the bladder is small, and it is located in the conduit of the rod, and fixed inside, and the urine cannot come out; then heal it as I say, that you cut it many times, this is an exception from cutting for this healing. I have proven this already.
Take a fork of iron according to this shape and have three prongs fixed in one stick:
then take a thread and tie it around the rod (i.e., urethra) beneath the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently insert the probe into the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the probe with your hand in the stone, pushing and pushing, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the rod. It will break immediately and exit along with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
And if you cannot do this because of some obstruction, then tie a thread beneath the stone and another above it; then make an incision in the rod (i.e., urethra) near the stone between the two ties; then extract it (i.e., the stone) and untie the thread; and clean the coagulated blood from the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
of the stone of women (i.e., a woman's kidney or bladder stone)
It rarely happens that a stone is passed by women, and if it does occur, the cure is difficult and is forbidden for three reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows herself well enough to reveal herself to the midwives, even when she is married.
And the third manner is that perhaps one cannot find a woman skilled enough in this art of midwifery; and the fourth manner is that the stone of the woman is often deeper than that of a man, for which reason it requires a deeper incision, causing great fear.
And if it is necessary to do so, you must summon a skilled midwife, but they are hard to find, and if you cannot find one, then take an honest and subtle married woman; and present her with a bowl of urine from the woman, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to carry out the examination for the stone as you have commanded.
And look carefully to see if the woman is a virgin: if she is, then you must insert your finger into her rectum and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she should press down on it with her finger and instruct the patient to push with her left hand on her bladder.
If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the entrance of the bladder to below, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then place a stone in the root of the thigh against the middle of the bone, where it is most prominent, and feel the stone in that spot; and do not move her hand above or below the stone, and make the incision shallow at first;
and push the artery into the incision, if you feel the stone growing larger, enlarge the wound until the stone can come out; and know that there are many types of stones: small and large, rough and smooth, long and round, with points or not; so recognize their appearances to know how to extract them.
And if the blood overcomes you, put vitriol powder in its place, and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, until the stone is out, and have the instruments with you that I mentioned in the extraction of stones in men to help you in your task.
And if the blood overcomes you, and it is from an artery that has been cut, put the powder in its place and apply pressure with bandages, and do not resume the procedure; and leave the stone where it is and do not pull it out, for the patient may die; then treat the wound.
And when the heat of the blood has calmed down and the place has cooled, return to your work, until the stone is out.
Of a carnous hernia
Ranice aquosa is nothing but a collection of moisture or white humor, which is under the skin of the groin and contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the egg, so that one thinks it is another egg; and this is the skin of the groin between the white humor that we have mentioned; and this does not happen unless a hernia is present.
And the formation of this ranice is due to weakness in the groin, and this material spreads out.
And sometimes it comes from percussion on the groin, and this moisture can have many different colors: it can turn yellowish, or be colorless, or black, or whitish, and this happens often.[Comments: Percussion here likely refers to an injury caused by a blunt object hitting the affected area. The different colors mentioned could refer to various states of inflammation or other medical conditions.]
and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white pus like we have said, then the abscess is ripe, that is, a long lump similar to an egg's shape, and the corners are not visible, because there is moisture all around.
And if there is moisture in the proper covering, then the abscess is ripe with part of the egg, and because of this, it is thought to be another egg.
And if the moisture is between the skin of the corners and the white pus, then it can be felt; therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, examine it with a probe that is four fingers wide, which is used for forming it.[](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/intromissoire) According to what follows the probe, then judge what is inside.
According to what follows the probe, then judge what is inside. And when we cure it with iron, the patient should be bled according to their ability and the fullness of their body; then have them lie on their back, on something a little high, and place many cloths beneath them.
Then have them sit on their left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on their right, and extend the rod to one of the two ribs of the loins;
Then take the scalpel and cut through the skin of the loins along its length down to the buttock, and let your incision be straight, dividing the skin of the loins until you reach the white fascia, and carefully remove the skin according to your ability;
Then make a full hole in the sac filled with water with a large perforation, and extract all the water, then place your fingers inside and pull the sac upwards; but do not touch the kidney, only the sac; cut away the covering of it very carefully, making sure to cut it thoroughly, for if you do not cut it deeply enough, the water will return.
And if the kidney slips out during your work, put it back in its place once you have completed the sac procedure; then sew up the two leaves of the renal fascia with a stitch, and cure it like any other wound until it is healed.[1](note: I made an assumption about what "l’uef" meant based on context)
And if you find the eye corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie up the vessels that are suspensive, in doubt of bloodletting; then cut the connection to all the suspensive vessels and remove the eye and cure it as we have said.
And if water has gathered in two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part similarly to how you did with the first, then wipe away the blood and put a woolen cloth soaked in rose oil into the wound.
and place on top another woolen cloth soaked in wine and oil, and put the two pieces of raw meat on top, and place folded cloths on top, and bind it all together with a bandage in this manner:
Then take two cloths and stuff them with loose wool in this manner and sew them together at the girdle of the breeches, and let one of the pieces support the buttocks up to the back, and the other on the side where the wound is, and the other two pieces on the two corners, and let all be tightly bound together with the belt of the breeches.[1](https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q375906)
And sometimes, this ramic cautery is used in place of an iron cut, and it is that you take a thin scalpel cautery, and cut the skin of the cheeks, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the whitish syfic (pus-filled blister) containing water is revealed;
take the cautery in this form, and pierce that syfic with the tip, and flay it with this thin, heated cautery;
And cut it in all ways that you can, as much as you reach everything; and make sure that the fire does not touch the yolk; and know that this work is safer; and pay attention to prevent bleeding, and be careful that it is not like the work of cutting.
And if anything opposes you, such as an abscess or bleeding or something else, then heal what is opposing you, according to what has been said before.
And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo the procedure due to its horror, perform perforation as I told you, that is: when you are completely certain, based on the signs we have mentioned, that the watery humor is present.
Have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess in its lower part over its entire width, and place the perforation through the length of the body; and let the opening be wide, so that all the watery humor may flow out.
Then place cotton on the wound and bandage it, allowing the remaining watery humor to drain out, and continue caring for the wound until it heals.
And if the white cloth does not allow the watery humor to drain out of the wound, you must insert a feather or the instrument used to drain the water from edematous patients, which has the shape described earlier; and widen one corner of the wound, knowing that the water will return, and collects again after six months or so. And when it collects as before, the patient will pass their days in this way.
of the abscess of the haunches/buttocks
Know that in the sectioning of this vein/vessel, there is fear in many cases, therefore it seems better to me to leave it alone.
and I will tell you the work and similarities of an abscess.
So I say that many abscesses come upon the body, and even upon the haunches/buttocks; and this is due to many causes.
That is to say, it comes from an acidic and sharp excess, which has spread to the haunches/buttocks, or from a blow/percussion.
and is the color of the abscess similar to the color of the skin; and there is no finding of pain, and it is a painful abscess;
and perhaps there is an abscess, painful and hard, of dark color, which sometimes comes from a ruptured artery or swelling of a vein.
When it is due to a ruptured artery, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess when you press it with your fingers.[ and one should not touch it at all.
He who is affected by inflammation of the vein can be recognized by its swelling upon touch of the fingers.
And one can easily perform the incision on this similar condition, and on other maladies. And it is necessary to cut the fat around the kidneys, then pull up the kidney and remove the white membrane from the surface, and free the suspensory ligament on all sides from the kidney.
If the kidneys are already hardened with these diseases, then it is necessary to remove the kidney and its membrane.
And if it is adhered to the membrane or in that which is inside the vessels, then one must free all the adhesions and cut around the kidney.[STH] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
And if the birth of the flesh is in that place, you should cut it all away and extract the egg, as we have said.
And when your work is completed, apply the wound with wet wool in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other cures until it is healed.

This is an abscess enclosed in a swelling resembling a hump, with the softening of the haunches (or: groins)[STHREE\_REQUESTS\_IN\_ONE](https://platform.openai.com/docs/api-reference/completions/create#completions/create-create-three-request-in-one) and the patient moves roughly when they walk;
and the treatment for this illness is as dangerous as the one mentioned before;
Nevertheless, we will tell you about its treatment, according to what the ancients did.[
You should make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then place the suspension device for the groin between your hands, close to the genitals, and the master pulls on them with force, stretching them out.
then cut with a sharp blade through the veins, until they are open,
and then flay from both sides, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples;
then insert a needle with two threads and tie it to the first place where the vein has come out, and then tie it again to the other end;[NOTE: I'm assuming "vis" is referring to the incision made in the veins earlier, as there are no explicit mention of a "vis" before.] then cut the middle parts evenly according to the length of the body, and remove the corrupt moisture;
then treat the wound like the others where blood flows, so that some of the veins remain intact to nourish one of the sides;
for if not, it does no harm, and if it comes to all the vessels, then one should draw out the corners (of the wound) in all the vessels; so that the bone does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry out and can no longer help (heal).
of the rupture of the syphilis sore. The outcome of this branch (of nerves) is due to the rupture that occurs in the syphilis sore or its extension on the abdomen in the region of the groin, causing the intestines to descend from that rupture towards one of the hips.
And this rupture occurs either in the syphilis sore or from its extension, and it results in two types of occurrences due to many causes: from impact, jumping, coughing, lifting heavy objects, and similar things.
And the signs when it is a stretching of the syfic are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and not suddenly; And the abscesses are even all the way to the depth because the syfic presses on the intestines.
And the sign is when it is a section of the syfic, that it brings about at the beginning sudden pain, and the abscesses are various in appearance, close to the skin, and this is because of the opening of the intestines and the body outside of the syfic.

of a carnal hernia
In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron (i.e., a surgical instrument).

Sometimes there comes a rupture in the intestines, as we have said, and the place becomes visible; and no part of the intestines descends to the groin, and if any does descend, it is little, and returns every hour;
And if it stays there for too long, the wound or abscess grows so large that the internal organs are exposed.
And this happens because of the swelling of the abscess which stretches the area, as we have said, for it becomes stretched, then softened and inflamed, and open.[inline end="true"]
And the treatment is by cauterization, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated with iron in this way:

of the softening of the skin of the buttocks.
Many times the skin of the buttocks is softened in some men, because the fat that is inside is softened, and it is obvious to see; and it is necessary, when one wants to cure it, that the patient be made to lie on their back, and cut the softened skin that is above the natural skin; then bring the two lips together with a suture, and if you see, first sew the excess softened skin with three or four firm stitches; then cut between the stitches, and cure it like the other wounds, until it is healed, and let the thread fall out.
of cautery/treatment.
Know that cautery is prohibited in our religion, and therefore I would not like to speak of it at all in this book; however, it is necessary for two reasons: one is so that the physician can give knowledgeable responses when asked about it and know how to perform the treatment; and the second reason is because we often need to use cautery on animals to help us, such as with goats, sheep, pigs, and other beasts. Therefore, I will say that cautery is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by incision.

of childbirth

of the fistula of the anus Fistulas that come from below the anus are hard and grow near the anus or in the space of the two parts (buttocks).
If there is one fistula or multiple, and when this hardening is old, it works (the fistula opens), and furthermore moisture appears, which is white pus or thin serous fluid.
And sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are recognized by the fact that there is a discharge or flatulence when the patient passes stool, and perhaps even in the form of worms.
And if there are fistulas that reach to the bladder, and to the middle of the penis; and they reach to the joint of the thigh, and to the groin.
And thus, one knows a fistula reaching to the anus, and not penetrating it. And this is done by inserting your index finger into the anus, and then carefully introducing a fine needle of steel or iron into the fistula when there is no tortuosity (twisting).

of wounds
We have already spoken in the division about the care of wounds; now we will tell you about the care of hands and of remedies, according to their implementation.[nos = we (plural)]
I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the locations where the wounds are made, and of what they are made.
The things by which wounds are made are: by striking with a stone, cutting with a sword and knife, or with a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things.
Or according to the parts of the body where wounds are located, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the chest, or the stomach, or the liver, and similar limbs.
And I will tell you the cure for each wound, starting with simple wounds of the head, for reminders will come in their own chapter
I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, pay attention if it is from striking with a stone or similar things, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large. and you should lightly incise for a hot abscess: do it immediately with the cephalic itself if it comes with little blood from the wound, and let the incision be opposite the injured part;
and let the patient abstain from wine and heavy meals.

Of the civilian vein

And know that it is not appropriate to tighten with stitches all the fractured members on the first day. For when the limb is large, it is not suitable to put in stitches except after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your certainty of abscess happening;
Here is the method of ancient emplasters to heal fractures, dislocations, and twisting: it consists of taking flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, and mixing it well with a large amount of egg, then using this preparation, neither too clear nor too thick, and applying it in this way. This is the common method of the restorative emplaster for healing fractures in various ways, and also for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Another method of the restorative emplaster for healing fractures, dislocations, and twisting: take three parts of costmary, ladanum, elecampane, asafoetida, gum arabic, and myrrh; each part is ten drams; and four drams each of myrrh and aloes; and grind them into a powder, then mix with egg yolk; if the person's complexion is hot, use this emplaster as it has a good composition and quickly restores broken bones, and it benefits many men.
Another method of the emplaster that is good for twisting: take myrrh and colt's foot, each ten drams; four drams each of aloes and acacia, eight drams of Armenian bole, grind well, and mix with water or egg yolk, then administer.
Another manner of poultice for joints and dislocated bones, to calm the resulting pain, and for healing broken bones: take new wool, and soak it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the spot. This poultice does not heal completely, but it is good for cooling down hot abscesses, and properly removing pains.
Another manner of poultice that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed broad-leaved thyme, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Another manner of poultice for the healing of bone fractures and reducing the remnants of abscesses: take root of althea, chamomile, violet flowers, bran, an equal amount of each; grind, mix with wine, and if the member is warm, moisten it with coriander water or plain water, and use.
Another stronger poultice than the previous one, when hard abscesses come to restore the member: take root of althea, seeds of flax, balm, sweet clover, violet flowers and chamomile, an equal amount of all; grind, mix with water of salt or plain water or with wine, depending on the warmth of the member and its rest.[ST1]
Hippocrates says in his book that one should not place anything on the broken member to restore it, except for a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be moderate in hardness, not too soft or too hard.
And it seems that Galen thinks that one should place on the broken member, to restore it, dry and slightly warm things, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Another form of poultice that is good for wounds and pain: take a dog's mouth and chopped off men's hair, or bird feathers, and chamomile, and equally, grind them, and make a poultice and apply it to the wound.
And then loosen it a little after, and make sure that the patient does not feel any pain or if the bone has not moved from its place, and do not unbind it for several days.
And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hasten, and unbind it, and remove the poultice now; and take a light cloth, and a sea sponge, and dip in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed down. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry linen on it, wet with water or rose oil, and bind it to a compress, until you are sure of a heated abscess.
And let the inflammation of the limb rest, and let the pain be removed, then begin the binding again, more lightly, and a little poultice, and do not bind it as tight as before; and carefully, until it is healed.
And if you see that the heated and red abscess and pain and swelling have all been removed, and you need poultice and bandages, then begin again as you did at first.
And if the member does not come to any of what we have said, do not unlock it before 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, so that the breaker is careful, and approaches the adjustment of the flesh on top;
Then restrain it more than before, and the flesh swells, as I said before; and if you see the place dry out more than necessary, know that healing cannot come. Therefore, it arises from hot wet swelling every time you unlock it, and this should be every third day, and loosen the binding a little.
Through this work, healing is delayed in the member, and it heals slowly what foolish surgeons do, who incorrectly set the member; this is bad, and it is a practice to be feared, and I see no other solution than to leave it alone and work correctly.
of the different ways of fracture There are many ways of fractures, and various shapes, and their causes are differentiated;
For there are fractures caused by sword blows, and the collarbone separates the entire bone down to the syphac which is beneath the bone, just like a hatchet or stick; and this type of fracture is called "haichure".
Or when the sword strikes the bone from above without penetrating, this type of fracture is called "absolue"; and the wound of these two fractures can be large or small.
And if there is an embedded impact, or a chip fracture, or a stone collar, or falling on a stone, or other similar things;
And if it has a fracture that reaches up to the membrane that is beneath the bone, or above the bone, and this wound is either large or small.
And if there is a wound that is sunken into the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called this fracture "hairline" or "capillary".
And if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or falling, or from similar causes, and it drives a piece of bone inward, and the place is uneven, like when coopers hammer on cauldrons; it goes inside the body.
And this happens more frequently in those who have moist bones in their head, such as the bones of children.
And this occurs in all types of fractures where small pieces are detached, like so; and I will speak about it further on.[ST1] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the withdrawal (traction) on them, and the investigation using tensors, and by the decayed flesh that is above.
A fracture is recognized by the appearance of hair when, after uncovering the bone and rubbing over it, a black line becomes visible.
In the treatment of fractures, be aware of the patient's condition and if you notice any adverse symptoms such as vomiting of bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, paleness, feverish chills, eyes turning out and becoming red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it is unlikely to heal without a doubt.
And if you do not see any alarming symptoms and expect a recovery, then begin the treatment.[nitpicky]
And when a wounded person first comes to you in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the month if possible.[nitpicky]
And if it is in the joint, hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone does not become rotten, and the complications that we mentioned come about.
And if the fracture of the bone reaches the membrane covering the brain, then you must cut open the split part in this way: that is, take hold of the head of the injured patient, and expose the bone as much as you can, in the shape of the wound as gently as possible.
And if bleeding occurs when the bone is exposed or an abscess arises, then help as appropriate and that is to fill the opening with cloths soaked in rose oil.[*](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/roset) And let the wound rest until the abscess has healed and you are sure that there is no more bleeding; then begin to remove the bone, and this can be done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and its shape is: ... (the text goes on to describe the incision)
And then put in another cut larger than the first one.
And the second manner is that you have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed, and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
And if the bone is hard and firm, then you must pierce it all around, so that you administer cuts with trephines, not so deep that they penetrate beyond the thickness of the skull, and there should be above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the tip to pass beyond the bone; and you need several of them, so that each one comes to rest in its place on the surface of the bone, so that you have trephines for all parts of the head; and this is the method of the three types of trephines.
The way to pierce around the bone is to place a trephine on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone is penetrated; then remove the trephine and place it in another spot nearby, and do this all around, then cut out the space of the skull between the holes with a chisel, doing this as delicately as possible and lightly, as we have said, so that you extract the bone by hand or with any of the tools that you have such as pliers or forceps; and be careful not to touch the brain or the dura mater.
And when you have penetrated and extracted the bone, then it is necessary that you clean the sharpness that remains from the bone with another tool resembling a chisel, but it should be thinner and more delicate than the other chisels.
and if there remains any fragments of small bones or splinters, then carefully remove them with one of the instruments; then cure the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
And the other method of work is that which Galen describes, which is safer; and he praises it highly, and this is his statement. First, it is necessary to uncover a portion of the bone in the place where the fracture is clearly visible. Once you have exposed that area, place the rounded tip of this surgical knife under the edge, as shown in its shape:
And do not make a cut all the way through on one side, rather leave it jagged in two edges so that the blade is alongside the bone. Then strike gently with a small mallet to lightly break the bone all around, taking great care of the cloth underneath.[...]
if it is loose from the bone, then remove it gently, for it can be easily removed without harm and fear.
And if the break of the bone does not penetrate through to the outer layer, and the bone is only cut through at the top, with small pieces, then you must smooth over that roughness, and remove the splinters with a sharp razor which you should have in various quantities, to make suitable adjustments in each place, according to the task and the shape of the break.
First use large razors, then smaller ones, and do not stop until it is smooth.
In each of the other haircutters and subtle breakers, it is necessary to make adjustments according to its alignment; and this is something that is not obvious to one who has devoted their study to this art.
And if the abscess is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound and soak it in rose oil and place it on the wound. then take another cloth, doubled in two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it on top of the first cloth; and do this as lightly as you can, so as not to harm the abscess, then apply another bandage on top, but don't pull it tight, just enough to hold the wound.
and leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess has calmed down, then loosen the bandage and apply medicine such as lily roots, vetches flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; make a powder from these and sprinkle it on the wound, then continue to apply painless medicine.
and make sure that the wound stays clean, not allowing any pus to accumulate or for it to become infected, because if pus forms under the cloth on the brain, it will rot and cause great harm to the patient; this is because when a painful substance is placed on the abscess, it causes necrosis.
Take care then, if any accident should befall the patient, as we have mentioned, it is doubtful without doubt.
And if no pus comes out unless due to the medicine that has been applied, which has such power, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and glue one bandage, and place it on the styptic. and treat it in various ways until it is healed.

And if the fracture is above the knee, and the bone cannot come into place, then you should align it even with the end of a rod that is slightly thick.
And if the fracture is in two parts, then do likewise (i.e. align it with a rod), and make haste to set it in place on the first day, if you are able;

Of the fracture of the jaw.
When the jawbone is fractured but there is no wound outside, and the break is external only, without being broken in two, except for a small piece inside, it can be easily recognized.
If the fracture is on the right side, then you should insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if it is on the left side, then insert your right hand's index finger, gently push the fracture inside, and align it with the other hand from the outside, making sure they are equal.
And if the fracture of the jaw is separated into two parts, then you must administer extension to both sides until they are equal.[SIMULATE] Me: How did medieval medical practitioners diagnose a fractured jawbone?

And if you see that the shape changes, then untie it on the third day, and then set right what has changed; and place a plaster on top, of powder from the mill with an abundance of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the compress; and place a light linen cloth on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it on until it heals; often it heals in three weeks.

And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as needed.
And when you have removed all those pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound if it is large, and apply a suitable poultice to it, to help heal the flesh until it is healed.

of the shoulder fracture
It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks or dislocates in such a way that it can be seen from the outside; one only knows this through touch. One should prepare the treatment according to the type of break and reposition it according to its natural shape, in all ways possible. Then put powdered flour mixed with egg white and light sponges on top, then a double layer of cloth. After that, place a wide and thin board over it, slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the board, fill them with linen sponges so that the board lies flat. Then bind it firmly all around with a long bandage, making sure that the board does not move from its place, and check the binding every day. And whenever it softens, tighten it again and make sure the board is in the right place, and have the patient lie on their side. The shoulder should be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is reached, untie it, and be careful because it is not an easy thing for the bone to come out of place.
And if a part of the bone juts out in front, but not beneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut as we have said in the breakage of the forearm to pacify a hot abscess.
In the break of the hip.
The thigh is sometimes broken in the middle, but that happens rarely; however, it often breaks at the end. And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and a lack of strength, and soon, and perhaps they vomit blood, and the fracture can be seen in the broken bone, and one can smell it easily.
The restoration is as follows: the patient lies down with their back on a cushion placed between their shoulders, then you should press their shoulders and bring together their ribs using your hands, making sure to align all parts of the bone correctly; afterwards, apply poultices and bandages soaked in saltwater or another light wood over the fracture, wrap it in a cloth, and secure it firmly over the broken bone so that it does not move; then tie a bandage around their back, tighten it appropriately, and check every hour to see if it needs to be tightened again; if it becomes necessary to loosen the bandage due to infection, itching, pain, or abscess, do so quickly, remove the poultice, treat the affected area as needed, reapply a new poultice, and secure it until healed.
of the breaking of ribs
Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about except in heavy blows to the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well upon examination of the sides.
And the setting consists of aligning the break properly, as is appropriate. Then apply the emplaster and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
And if the breaking of ribs leans inward, then the patient feels great pain and distress, just like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the skin; and there is sharp pain when breathing, and immediately there is a large flow of blood, which is a serious matter. Ancient physicians have applied much skill to this problem.
And some say that one must administer food that causes the belly to swell in order to push the break outward.[0](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/aministrer)
We do not make it so that abscesses come to a boil, if they have not already come. And if it has come to a head, then lance it.
And some say that one should apply cups to the place in order to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups may attract impurities to the place due to its weak constitution.
And some say that one should cover the place with a cloth soaked in hot oil and then place bandages between the ribs to evenly apply pressure around, and then let it be treated with the treatment for pleurisy, food, and medicine.
And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone pressing against the cloth, and if the patient is anxious, then you must make an incision on the place where the rib is broken, and place a device underneath to protect the lung; and then you should cut the bone, and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and dress it with poultices until it heals. And if an abscess comes, then put wet bandages soaked in rose oil on the area, and place them on the patient; and treat the place as one does for an abscess, and keep the patient lying on their side on the rib where they must lie, until it heals.
of the break/fracture of the neck
Sometimes there occurs a break/fracture in the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back. And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, look to see if you notice their hands are softened, swollen, and without feeling, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that in many cases, this means they are mortally injured, but if they can move them and feel when they are pressed or poked, know that the joints of the bone are safe, and that the patient will recover if treated.[Reference(s):
And if similar things happen in the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will recover or not, look to see if the feet are soft, and if there are symptoms in the hands, and on the back there is windiness and involuntary evacuation; and when it is turned onto its stomach, there is still involuntary evacuation. And when it is turned onto its back and wants to sit up, it cannot. Know that it is mortal: do not even attempt to cure it.[Reference(s):
And if these symptoms do not occur, then it is a less severe condition.[Reference(s):
And the cure is that you should do if there is a hot abscess, place on it rose oil or egg yolk oil, until it is calmed down; then place one of the warming and drying plasters on it, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain, until it is healed. And if any bone becomes dislocated, it is necessary to cover the area with a compress; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with one stitch, then cure it with a healing ointment, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", place your left hand pocket on it, and push it into place with your right hand to the best of your ability, then apply the plaster and bandage if needed; then bind it, and if there is a dislocated bone, adjust it and remove it, and cure the wound until it is healed.
of the fracture of the thigh bone.
It often happens that the thigh bone is broken, and if it does, it rarely results in much narrowing at the end; it bends long and inclines outward, and causes pain to the patient in that area, and swelling and bruising in the area where it is broken.
And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand on top, so that you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the head only, then align that break equally, so that it is in its natural shape.

of the shoulder joint breakage
The shoulder joint is what lies between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it must be restored according to one of the two methods: one of which is that you take a rod of medium size, in this shape:
And tie the two ends of the shoulder joint with two bandages and pull them upwards, and place the patient on a seat; then let him rest his broken arm on the rod, so that it is in the middle of a bow-shaped piece of wood, then suspend it from some heavy object or have the attendant stretch it downward; then bring the two ends of the break together with your hands until the break returns to its proper position.
And the other manner is to position the patient on his backside, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants to hold either end of the broken bone with their hands, one holding the part above the break, and the other holding the part below, each pulling in their direction.
And if you wish the extraction to be stronger, tie one ligament below the break and another above it, and have each assistant pull in their direction. And if the break is close to the top of the shoulder, place one ligament in the middle below the armpit, and another towards the side, below the break; and do the same if the break is towards the side. Then align the break as it should be, and apply even tension, if no abscesses form.
And if abscesses do form, then do not apply tension for seven days, and place a wet linen cloth soaked in rose oil on the affected area. Wait until the abscess has calmed down, then apply tension. The method of applying tension is to place the poultice on the break, align the arm with the shoulder or chest, and place your hand on the shoulder or chest. Then place a cloth and apply tension on the shoulder and arm, so that the arm remains in its natural position, if nothing prevents it, and unless the bones are misaligned.
And if you are unsure whether the bones are misaligned, use a splint and place a wider and stronger rod over the break than the others, with a space of two fingers between each rod. Each rod should be large enough to extend beyond the break by three fingers on either side. Then apply tension to the rods as I described at the beginning of this chapter, more firmly and less gradually.[Additional context: This passage describes the use of a splint to stabilize and align a fractured bone before applying tension.]
And if you see the swelling and tightening, as we have said, at the time you restore the broken member, and you doubt a hot abscess, then let it be bound up until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the binding every three days to see if itching, inflammation, or discharge comes to the place, or if circulation cannot reach the member because the binding is too tight. Loosen it, as we have said.
And if no such accidents occur, then do not loosen it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; and place a cushion full of evenly spread wool underneath them. Look every hour of the day and night to see if the shape of the broken member changes or if the binding has become too loose; then adjust it by the power of medicine, and give the patient the food that we mentioned before, in such a way that the food is initially fine; and when they begin to recover, make it coarse. And it is customary for the binding and leg to be recovered in 40 days in total; and then one should unbind and administer baths and ointment medications to straighten the place. And if the stricture is severe and embedded, then delay unbinding for one day or two months.
Here's the translation of the text you provided in Old French about the treatment for a broken arm:
The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fosicles", one of which is small and is the one that follows the thumb; and the other is large and is the one that is below, towards the little finger; it may happen that only the large fosicle breaks, or only the small one, and sometimes both together.
When the small ribs are broken, the restoration and healing is easy; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult and more severe than when they are both broken together. If it is only the small rib that is broken, then it should be lightly stretched and aligned.

of hip dislocations
Know that at the joints of the groin and the shoulder, there come only dislocations, not like the other joints; and the joint of the groin is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside than elsewhere, and less dislocated in front and back.
And the recognition of its internal dislocation is that when the sick leg is joined with the healthy one, it is longer, and the sick knee appears more open than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee over the fire. And the signs of this that occurs to him in the back, is that he cannot straighten his knee or bend it, and one leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the groin on the side of the loins is affected.

of the dislocation of the knee.
The knee dislocates in three ways: namely, inside and outside, and backward; it does not dislocate in front.
And the signs are that you tell the patient to bend his leg to his thigh, and if it doesn't reach his thigh, know that it is dislocated.
And the restoration of all (dislocations) is that you make the patient sit upright, and stretch out his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and place his foot on top of your feet.
Then take his knee in your palms, and pull it towards you between your hands, then bend the two sides of the knee strongly; and another minister extends his foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he can easily join his leg to his thigh.
And apply the poultice on it, and heat the leg to the thigh, and bandage the limb strongly together for three or four days, then loosen it; and do not let the patient move around until the limb is healed.
And if the limb is not healthy yet, administer a strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of inflammation, until it is healed.
of the dislocation of the heel.
The heel is sometimes dislocated, and sometimes fully dislocated, both inward and outward.
And the signs of this are that the ankle is swollen, and it tilts towards the side where it is dislocated.
The reduction is easy, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is only dislocated.
And when it is fully dislocated, you should have the patient sit upright, and have one assistant firmly hold their leg above the ankle.
then pull the foot toward you with your right hand, and then two times with your left hand, then stretch it upwards, and properly put the foot upward;
